<p><i><b>Magna Carta Holy Grail</b></i> (stylized as <i><b>Magna Carta... Holy Grail</b></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> is the twelfth <a href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album" class="mw-redirect">studio album</a> by American rapper <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>. It was made available for free <a href="/wiki/Music_download" title="Music download">digital download</a> for <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a> customers via the Jay Z Magna Carta <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">app</a> on July 4, 2013. It was then released for retail sale on July 8, 2013, by <a href="/wiki/Roc-A-Fella_Records" title="Roc-A-Fella Records">Roc-A-Fella</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a> while being distributed by <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Distribution" title="Universal Music Distribution">Universal</a>. It features <a href="/wiki/Guest_appearance" title="Guest appearance">guest appearances</a> by <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Ocean" title="Frank Ocean">Frank Ocean</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>. Most of the album was produced by <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a> and <a href="/wiki/J-Roc_(record_producer)" title="J-Roc (record producer)">Jerome "J-Roc" Harmon</a>, while other producers included <a href="/wiki/Boi-1da" title="Boi-1da">Boi-1da</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Will_Made_It" title="Mike Will Made It">Mike Will Made It</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hit-Boy" title="Hit-Boy">Hit-Boy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Dean_(record_producer)" title="Mike Dean (record producer)">Mike Dean</a>, <a href="/wiki/No_ID" title="No ID" class="mw-redirect">No ID</a>, <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> among others.The album was promoted through various commercials presented by Samsung and was not preceded by any retail singles.</p>
<p>Upon its release <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> was met with mixed reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>, who were divided in their opinion about the album. Some critics complimented the production and composition of the album, while others were disappointed with the overall theme and the repetitive nature of the songs. On the day of its physical release in the United States, the album was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">Platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) for shipments of 1,000,000 copies. It debuted at number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, selling 528,000&#160;copies in its first week, making it Jay-Z's 13th consecutive studio album to top the chart. On September 2, 2013, it was announced that <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> was certified double Platinum by the RIAA, for shipments of two million copies in the United States. The album was nominated in six categories at the <a href="/wiki/56th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="56th Annual Grammy Awards">2014 Grammy Awards</a> winning the Best Rap/Sung Collaboration trophy for "<a href="/wiki/Holy_Grail_(Jay-Z_song)" title="Holy Grail (Jay-Z song)">Holy Grail</a>" featuring Justin Timberlake.</p>
<p>The album spawned three successful singles, "<a href="/wiki/Holy_Grail_(Jay-Z_song)" title="Holy Grail (Jay-Z song)">Holy Grail</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Tom_Ford_(song)" title="Tom Ford (song)">Tom Ford</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Part_II_(On_the_Run)" title="Part II (On the Run)">Part II (On the Run)</a>" featuring Beyoncé. Multiple other songs on the album achieved chart success including, "<a href="/wiki/FuckWithMeYouKnowIGotIt" title="FuckWithMeYouKnowIGotIt">FuckWithMeYouKnowIGotIt</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Oceans_(Jay-Z_song)" title="Oceans (Jay-Z song)">Oceans</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Heaven_(Jay-Z_song)" title="Heaven (Jay-Z song)">Heaven</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Picasso_Baby" title="Picasso Baby">Picasso Baby</a>". Additionally, the album was supported by the <a href="/wiki/Concert_tour" title="Concert tour" class="mw-redirect">concert tour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magna_Carter_World_Tour" title="Magna Carter World Tour">Magna Carter World Tour</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Certifications"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Certifications</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Release_history"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Release history</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magna_Carta_Holy_Grail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On September 23, 2010, rapper <a href="/wiki/Q-Tip_(rapper)" title="Q-Tip (rapper)" class="mw-redirect">Q-Tip</a> confirmed working on Jay-Z's twelfth studio album, with a tentative release in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> By May 2012, reports arose that he was working on new music with <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a> producer <a href="/wiki/Jahlil_Beats" title="Jahlil Beats">Jahlil Beats</a>. In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a></i>, Beats stated: "Me and Jay-Z been going back and forth. He picked a couple of my joints that he’s working on. I don’t even wanna say too much about Jay, but we definitely working on some stuff. I haven’t even sent him a bunch of beats. I sent him my favorite stuff. He hit me right back like, ‘Yo, I’ma go in on this,’ or, ‘I like this.’”<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> The album development was kept a secret, but <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a> hinted about a new Jay-Z album in an April 2013 interview with <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-albumannouncement_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-albumannouncement-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Leading up to the album's announcement, Jay-Z served as an executive producer for both the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Gatsby_(2013_film)" title="The Great Gatsby (2013 film)">The Great Gatsby</a></i> and its <a href="/wiki/Soundtrack" title="Soundtrack">soundtrack</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Gatsby:_Music_from_Baz_Luhrmann%27s_Film" title="The Great Gatsby: Music from Baz Luhrmann's Film">The Great Gatsby: Music from Baz Luhrmann's Film</a></i>, which he and <a href="/wiki/Film_director" title="Film director">film director</a> <a href="/wiki/Baz_Luhrmann" title="Baz Luhrmann">Baz Luhrmann</a> worked together for two years .<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Makarechi_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makarechi-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Young_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Young-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The opening song, "100$ Bill" by Jay-Z contains a <a href="/wiki/Chopped_and_screwed" title="Chopped and screwed">chopped and screwed</a> beat, electro-rap elements and is written in the perspective of a modern-day Gatsby, it was both co-written and produced by <a href="/wiki/E*vax" title="E*vax">E*vax</a> one half of <a href="/wiki/Electronic_rock" title="Electronic rock">electronic rock</a> duo <a href="/wiki/Ratatat" title="Ratatat">Ratatat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-newsday_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsday-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vibemag_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vibemag-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording_and_production">Recording and production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magna_Carta_Holy_Grail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording and production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Timbaland1292010.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Timbaland1292010.png/180px-Timbaland1292010.png" width="180" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Timbaland1292010.png/270px-Timbaland1292010.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Timbaland1292010.png/360px-Timbaland1292010.png 2x" data-file-width="364" data-file-height="379" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Timbaland1292010.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a> provided the bulk of the <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_production" title="Hip hop production">production</a> on the album.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In late 2011, it was confirmed three songs had been recorded and one of which featured <a href="/wiki/Frank_Ocean" title="Frank Ocean">Frank Ocean</a> which would end up being "<a href="/wiki/Oceans_(Jay-Z_song)" title="Oceans (Jay-Z song)">Oceans</a>", the oldest song that appeared on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The recording for "Oceans" and production for "<a href="/wiki/Holy_Grail_(Jay-Z_song)" title="Holy Grail (Jay-Z song)">Holy Grail</a>" were completed in 2011, during the recording sessions for Jay's collaborative album with <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Watch_the_Throne" title="Watch the Throne">Watch the Throne</a></i>. West wanted the two songs to appear on <i>Watch the Throne</i>, however Jay-Z chose to keep them for <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-hhdx_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hhdx-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> After <i>Watch the Throne</i> was released, Jay-Z chose to go on a worldwide concert tour instead of devoting more time for the album. Following the end of the tour, the main bulk of recording sessions for <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> took place at <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a>' Jungle City Studios in New York, where <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_Knowles" title="Beyoncé Knowles" class="mw-redirect">Beyoncé Knowles</a> were also working on their albums at the time. Jay-Z described the recording process as having a "minimalist approach" to give <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> a "1990s feel".<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While working on Beyoncé's <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_(album)" title="Beyoncé (album)">fifth studio album</a>, frequent collaborator <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a> played Jay-Z the instrumental for what would become "<a href="/wiki/Picasso_Baby" title="Picasso Baby">Picasso Baby</a>". According to Jay-Z, that song built the sound of the album. Jay-Z and Timbaland had grew apart after they worked on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Blueprint_3" title="The Blueprint 3">The Blueprint 3</a></i>, but reunited for this album. Timbaland ended up handling the majority of the production on <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i>. In an interview with <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a>, Jay-Z stated that while the two have recorded many songs in the past, it was not until <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> that they got the chemistry to collaborate for a whole project.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Producer <a href="/wiki/Jerome_%22J-Roc%22_Harmon" title="Jerome &quot;J-Roc&quot; Harmon" class="mw-redirect">J-Roc</a> described "Picasso Baby" as "just New York". He told <i>XXL</i> that him and Timbaland "were really just feeling the city, the energy that it gives out" and were inspired by the "numerous different cultures and different dialects or sounds."<sup id="cite_ref-xxl-5p_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-5p-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Justin_Timberlake_2011_AA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Justin_Timberlake_2011_AA.jpg/160px-Justin_Timberlake_2011_AA.jpg" width="160" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Justin_Timberlake_2011_AA.jpg/240px-Justin_Timberlake_2011_AA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Justin_Timberlake_2011_AA.jpg/320px-Justin_Timberlake_2011_AA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1697" data-file-height="1533" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Justin_Timberlake_2011_AA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf6/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a> makes three appearances on the album.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The instrumental for "<a href="/wiki/FuckWithMeYouKnowIGotIt" title="FuckWithMeYouKnowIGotIt">FuckWithMeYouKnowIGotIt</a>" was started by producer Vinylz, who was inspired by a <a href="/wiki/Pimp_C" title="Pimp C">Pimp C</a> speech he found on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>. He sampled Pimp C's voice for the intro and then created the instrumental in a short amount of time. After fellow producer <a href="/wiki/Boi-1da" title="Boi-1da">Boi-1da</a> added to the production, the song was sent to <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a> who intended to use it for his upcoming album. Jay-Z was meant to add a guest verse to it, but when he heard the instrumental, he wanted the track for his album. Timbaland added additional changes to it before they mastered the final version.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl-5p_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-5p-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, Jay-Z contacted <a href="/wiki/GOOD_Music" title="GOOD Music">GOOD Music</a> producer <a href="/wiki/Hit-Boy" title="Hit-Boy">Hit-Boy</a> about working together on <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i>. Hit-Boy created the instrumental for "Somewhereinamerica", a song that was initially supposed to appear on the debut album of GOOD Music artist <a href="/wiki/Travis_Scott_(rapper)" title="Travis Scott (rapper)" class="mw-redirect">Travis Scott</a>. While in the studio with Jay-Z, Scott played the instrumental for him and Jay-Z instantly liked it.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl-sia_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-sia-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The instrumental for the song "Crown" was made by 16-year-old Canadian producer WondaGurl. She had collaborated with Travis Scott on his <i><a href="/wiki/Owl_Pharaoh" title="Owl Pharaoh">Owl Pharaoh</a></i> mixtape and went on to produce another track for his upcoming album. Scott liked the instrumental and started to build upon it with <a href="/wiki/Mike_Dean_(record_producer)" title="Mike Dean (record producer)">Mike Dean</a>. The two then gave it to Jay-Z who recorded "Crown" over it.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl-5p_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-5p-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Overall, Jay-Z worked extensively on the album's production with producers such as <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a>, Timbaland and <a href="/wiki/Pharrell_Williams" title="Pharrell Williams">Pharrell Williams</a> who were also featured in the Samsung commercials promoting <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i>. He had also worked on the album's production with <a href="/wiki/Jahlil_Beats" title="Jahlil Beats">Jahlil Beats</a>, Boi-1da, Mike Dean, <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Will_Made_It" title="Mike Will Made It">Mike Will Made It</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mtvhive1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtvhive1-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> He had also been seen in the studio with various recording artists such as <a href="/wiki/Drake_(rapper)" title="Drake (rapper)">Drake</a>, <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raekwon" title="Raekwon">Raekwon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, and Timberlake working on the album.<sup id="cite_ref-albumannouncement_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-albumannouncement-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> The final track listing revealed guest appearances by Timberlake, Frank Ocean, Nas, Pharrell, Swizz Beatz, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Ross" title="Rick Ross">Rick Ross</a> and Beyoncé among others.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_and_promotion">Release and promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magna_Carta_Holy_Grail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Release and promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Magna_Carter_World_Tour" title="Magna Carter World Tour">Magna Carter World Tour</a></div>
<p>On June 16, 2013, during the fifth game of the <a href="/wiki/2013_NBA_Finals" title="2013 NBA Finals">2013 NBA Finals</a>, Jay-Z was featured in a new commercial by <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a> where he announced that his twelfth studio album would be titled, <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> and would be released on July 4, 2013. He was seen speaking to producer <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin" title="Rick Rubin">Rick Rubin</a> in the studio about the album saying, "[It] is about, like this duality of how do you navigate through this whole thing, through success, through failures, through all this and remain yourself." The commercial featured producers that are confirmed to be on the album including Timbaland, Swizz Beatz and Pharrell Williams. The album was made available for free download on July 4, 12:01 a.m. EST, to the first one million <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S_III" title="Samsung Galaxy S III">Samsung Galaxy S III</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S4" title="Samsung Galaxy S4">Samsung Galaxy S4</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_Note_II" title="Samsung Galaxy Note II">Samsung Galaxy Note II</a> users of a new app.<sup id="cite_ref-albumannouncement_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-albumannouncement-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Shortly after, <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> said that the Samsung deal would not count towards the sales figures used by <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> to compile their charts.<sup id="cite_ref-sales_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sales-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was then released for retail sale three days later, on July 7, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Leading up to the release of the album, Jay-Z released selected lyrics of each song daily, via the Samsung app. This included "<a href="/wiki/Holy_Grail_(Jay-Z_song)" title="Holy Grail (Jay-Z song)">Holy Grail</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Heaven_(Jay-Z_song)" title="Heaven (Jay-Z song)">Heaven</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Oceans_(Jay-Z_song)" title="Oceans (Jay-Z song)">Oceans</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Part_II_(On_the_Run)" title="Part II (On the Run)">Part II (On the Run)</a>", "BBC", "Jay Z Blue", "Versus", "La Familia", "Tom Ford", "Beach Is Better", "Crown", "<a href="/wiki/Picasso_Baby" title="Picasso Baby">Picasso Baby</a>", "F.U.T.W.", "Nickels &amp; Dimes" and "SomewhereInAmerica" in order.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> On July 3, 2013, the cover art of the album was revealed in a photo where it was placed next to the one of the four surviving copies of album's namesake (<a href="/wiki/Magna_Carta" title="Magna Carta">the 13th-century English charter</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Salisbury_Cathedral" title="Salisbury Cathedral">Salisbury Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, and it remained on display there until the end of July.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-coverart_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coverart-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The logo for the album was inspired by an art piece by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Be_Andr&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Be Andr (page does not exist)">Be Andr</a> from 2009 named ‘Untitled (art)’.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2013_Grammy_Awards" title="2013 Grammy Awards" class="mw-redirect">2013 Grammy Awards</a>, Timberlake and Jay-Z performed their hit single "<a href="/wiki/Suit_%26_Tie" title="Suit &amp; Tie">Suit &amp; Tie</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-announcement_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-announcement-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Following their appearance on Grammys, rumors of a stadium tour between the artists were raised as a result of Jay-Z's posts on his Life + Times website; he posted series of venues with the note "#LegendsOfSummer this week".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Legends_of_the_Summer_Stadium_Tour" title="Legends of the Summer Stadium Tour" class="mw-redirect">Legends of the Summer Stadium Tour</a> was officially announced on February 22, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-announcement_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-announcement-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour begun on July 14, 2013 in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, England.<sup id="cite_ref-announcement_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-announcement-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Starting in October 2013, Jay-Z toured Europe on the <a href="/wiki/Magna_Carter_World_Tour" title="Magna Carter World Tour">Magna Carter World Tour</a>. It begun on October 3 at the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Arena" title="Manchester Arena">Manchester Arena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, England and concluded on October 29 at the <a href="/wiki/Ziggo_Dome" title="Ziggo Dome">Ziggo Dome</a> in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> The North American leg followed that, and it ended on January 31, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magna_Carta_Holy_Grail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On April 11, 2013, Jay-Z released the first song from the album titled "Open Letter". The song was a response to the critics of his fifth wedding anniversary that took place in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. This was due to the current <a href="/wiki/United_States_embargo_against_Cuba" title="United States embargo against Cuba">United States embargo against Cuba</a>, which required them needing a permit to visit the country.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was produced by <a href="/wiki/Swizz_Beatz" title="Swizz Beatz">Swizz Beatz</a>, and was included on the album as a bonus track. On July 10, 2013, <a href="/wiki/Third_Man_Records" title="Third Man Records">Third Man Records</a> announced on their website that they had entered a deal to release <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> on <a href="/wiki/LP_record" title="LP record">vinyl</a>, also confirming that "Open Letter" would be included as a vinyl-only bonus track and that there would be "something [else] very special planned for the vinyl edition."<sup id="cite_ref-thirdman_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thirdman-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the 'vinyl-only' appearance of "Open Letter" has been shown to not apply to all market areas.<sup id="cite_ref-AU_CD_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AU_CD-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Third Man Records is set to issue "Open Letter" in the form of a <a href="/wiki/Gramophone_record" title="Gramophone record">vinyl single</a> designed as a playable letter.<sup id="cite_ref-Exclaim_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exclaim-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a>, Jay-Z went into detail about the single's release, saying: "It's in a letter. You can play the letter. It's amazing... You open the letter, and you can actually play the card."<sup id="cite_ref-Exclaim_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exclaim-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The song "<a href="/wiki/Holy_Grail_(Jay-Z_song)" title="Holy Grail (Jay-Z song)">Holy Grail</a>" features vocals from singer Justin Timberlake and served as the album's first single<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> being serviced as a single to radio in the UK starting on July 10, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> It was produced by <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a>, Timbaland and Jerome "J-Roc" Harmon, with additional production from <a href="/wiki/No_ID" title="No ID" class="mw-redirect">No ID</a> and containing elements of <a href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)" title="Nirvana (band)">Nirvana</a>'s 1991 hit single "<a href="/wiki/Smells_Like_Teen_Spirit" title="Smells Like Teen Spirit">Smells Like Teen Spirit</a>". Following the release of the album, the song debuted at number eight on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> and number 24 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uk_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uk-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The song has since peaked at number four on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-SinglesUSPeaks_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SinglesUSPeaks-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The music video was released on August 29, 2013, making social media history as the first time a clip from major artists debuted strictly on <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On September 26, 2013, the album's second single "<a href="/wiki/Tom_Ford_(song)" title="Tom Ford (song)">Tom Ford</a>" was serviced to <a href="/wiki/Urban_contemporary" title="Urban contemporary">urban contemporary</a> radio in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and then on October 15, 2013, to <a href="/wiki/Rhythmic_contemporary" title="Rhythmic contemporary">rhythmic contemporary</a> in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-USRadioRelease_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USRadioRelease-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Prior to its single release, the song peaked at number 39 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SinglesUSPeaks_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SinglesUSPeaks-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Part_II_(On_the_Run)" title="Part II (On the Run)">Part II (On the Run)</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_Knowles" title="Beyoncé Knowles" class="mw-redirect">Beyoncé</a> was serviced to <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_hit_radio" title="Contemporary hit radio">contemporary hit radio</a> stations on February 18, 2014 as the album's third single.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The song has since peaked at number 80 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-SinglesUSPeaks_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SinglesUSPeaks-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magna_Carta_Holy_Grail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and sold 528,000 copies in its first week, which bypassed its predicted debut in the range of 350,000 to 400,000.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard-debut_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-debut-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The album also debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>. It is Jay-Z's third straight number one album in Canada. The album debuted at number one on the UK Album Chart, Jay-Z's first UK number one album. In its second week the album sold 129,000 more copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite the 76% drop in sales, <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> retained its number one position on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, becoming the first rap album to spend two consecutive weeks on top since <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Tha_Carter_IV" title="Tha Carter IV">Tha Carter IV</a></i> (2011).<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> In its third week the album would drop down to number two, selling 77,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> In its fourth week the album would drop down to number three, selling 62,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> It sold 1,099,000 copies in 2013 in the United States, making it the tenth best-selling albums of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-sales_2013_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sales_2013-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> By February 26, 2014, the album had sold 1,130,000 copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> As of September 2, 2013, It was announced by <i>Billboard</i> that <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certifications" title="RIAA certifications" class="mw-redirect">double platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), for shipments of two million copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At the time of its release, the album had the second-biggest sales week for 2013, behind Justin Timberlake's <i><a href="/wiki/The_20/20_Experience" title="The 20/20 Experience">The 20/20 Experience</a></i>. <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i>'s debut marked the first time in <i>Billboard'</i>s history when four different rap albums have consecutively spent weeks at number one, after <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Yeezus" title="Yeezus">Yeezus</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Wale_(rapper)" title="Wale (rapper)">Wale</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Gifted" title="The Gifted">The Gifted</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Born_Sinner" title="Born Sinner">Born Sinner</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard-debut_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-debut-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> also became Jay-Z's 13th studio album in a row to top the <i>Billboard</i> 200, extending his record for the most chart-toppers by a solo act in <i>Billboard</i>'s history.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard-debut_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-debut-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magna_Carta_Holy_Grail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="vertical-align:middle">5/10<sup id="cite_ref-Sargent_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sargent-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></td>

<p><i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> received generally mixed reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>. At <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">normalized</a> rating out of 100 to reviews from critics, the album received an <a href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean" class="mw-redirect">average</a> score of 60, based on 42 reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> In his review for <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Pareles" title="Jon Pareles">Jon Pareles</a> wrote that Jay-Z is trying to transition from <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> but has not yet found a "reliable alternative", and that his raps are often mismatched with rigidly produced tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-Pareles_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pareles-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a>'s Andy Kellman felt that the album was hastily produced and that, despite occasionally impressive lyrics, Jay-Z's pop culture references sound reflexive.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> magazine's Jordan Sargent said that the songs sound both too elaborate and unfinished, and have similar but less momentous themes as <i><a href="/wiki/Watch_the_Throne" title="Watch the Throne">Watch the Throne</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sargent_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sargent-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a>'s Jesse Cataldo viewed <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> as a self-important album marred by shallow <a href="/wiki/Name-dropping" title="Name-dropping">name-dropping</a> and accused Jay-Z of becoming disinterested creatively because of his increased success.<sup id="cite_ref-slant_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slant-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Evan Rytlewski of <i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i> said that he exhausts the ending of his <a href="/wiki/Rags_to_riches" title="Rags to riches">rags to riches</a> narrative and cannot reinvent himself beyond gloating superficially about his riches.<sup id="cite_ref-avclub_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-avclub-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i><span style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Helen Brown found his boastful references heavy-handed and the album unchallenging, albeit enjoyable for "the lazy listener".<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Greg_Kot" title="Greg Kot">Greg Kot</a>, writing in the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i>, viewed that, apart from well-written moments on "Oceans", "Jay-Z Blue", and "Nickel &amp; Dimes", most of the album is inconsequential.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a positive review, Randall Roberts of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> was impressed by the production's energy and effective samples, even though he thought the album is not as intellectual or adventurous as its title suggests.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Uncut_(magazine)" title="Uncut (magazine)">Uncut</a></i> wrote that it mostly succeeds as Jay-Z's attempt to "balance his great wealth, tough history and news responsibility while retaining his grit."<sup id="cite_ref-uncut_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uncut-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Louis Pattison of <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> said that it lacks a radical presence such as Kanye West to complement Jay-Z's mature ruminations, but still shows him as a sagacious lyricist comparable with <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nme_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nme-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kitty_Empire" title="Kitty Empire">Kitty Empire</a>, writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i>, believed that the diverse production will initially draw listeners rather than Jay-Z's predictably "umpteenth retelling" of his rags-to-riches story, but the topics become more interesting on subsequent listens because of his surprisingly concerned takes on fatherhood and charity.<sup id="cite_ref-Empire_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Empire-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> In his review for <a href="/wiki/MSN_Music" title="MSN Music">MSN Music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> said that he was won over after several listens by the familial songs, which he found amusing on an album that pits "black man as artistic rebel versus black man as family stalwart".<sup id="cite_ref-christgau_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-christgau-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magna_Carta_Holy_Grail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Closing out the year, <i>Magna Carta Holy Grail</i> was met with many accolades and was named in multiple "Albums of the Year" lists by major publications. It was nominated for Album of the Year at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/BET_Hip_Hop_Awards" title="BET Hip Hop Awards">BET Hip Hop Awards</a><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> and for Best Rap Album at the <a href="/wiki/56th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="56th Annual Grammy Awards">56th Annual Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" title="Complex (magazine)">Complex</a></i> ranked the album at number 23, on their list of the 50 best albums of 2013. They praised the "high-gloss production," and strong rhymes by Jay-Z, deeming it "very listenable".<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> named it the tenth best hip hop album of the 2013 saying, "The legendary MC explored of-the-moment sounds, textures and tempos in ways only he could [...] Even on a bit of an off day, Jay is still plenty impressive."<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> It was named the eighth best album of 2013 by <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<tr>
<th>Year</th>

<td>Top Rap Album</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Track_listing">Track listing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magna_Carta_Holy_Grail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Track listing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">"Open Letter" &#160;</td>

<dl>
<dt>Notes</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_a">^a</a></b></span></sup> signifies an additional <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">producer</a>.</li>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_b"><b><a href="#ref_b">^b</a></b></span></sup> signifies a co-producer.</li>
<li><sup><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_c"><b><a href="#ref_c">^c</a></b></span></sup> signifies an additional <a href="/wiki/Programming_(music)" title="Programming (music)">programmer</a>.</li>
<li>"Somewhereinamerica" is alternatively spelled as "Somewhere in America" in some versions of the album.<sup id="cite_ref-iTunes-au_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iTunes-au-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"Holy Grail" features additional vocals by The-Dream.</li>
<li>"Picasso Baby" features additional vocals by The-Dream and <a href="/wiki/Jean_Reno#Personal_life" title="Jean Reno">Zofia Borucka Moreno</a>.</li>
<li>"Tom Ford" features additional vocals by Beyoncé Knowles who is credited as "Third Ward Trill".</li>
<li>"Crown" features additional vocals by Travis Scott.</li>
<li>"Heaven" features additional vocals by Justin Timberlake.</li>
<li>"BBC" features additional vocals by <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, Pharrell, Timbaland, Justin Timberlake, Swizz Beatz and Beyoncé Knowles who is credited as "Third Ward Trill".</li>
<li>"Jay Z Blue" features additional vocals by Taffy.</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Samples</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>"Holy Grail" contains elements of "<a href="/wiki/Smells_Like_Teen_Spirit" title="Smells Like Teen Spirit">Smells Like Teen Spirit</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)" title="Nirvana (band)">Nirvana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-complex1_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex1-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"Picasso Baby" contains a sample of "Sirens" by <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Younge" title="Adrian Younge">Adrian Younge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-xxlmag1_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxlmag1-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"Tom Ford" contains elements of "<a href="/wiki/Bad_Girls_(M.I.A._song)" title="Bad Girls (M.I.A. song)">Bad Girls</a>" by <a href="/wiki/M.I.A._(artist)" title="M.I.A. (artist)" class="mw-redirect">M.I.A.</a></li>
<li>"Somewhereinamerica" embodies portions of "Gangster of Love (Part 1)" written by Johnny Guitar Watson.<sup id="cite_ref-xxlmag1_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxlmag1-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"Crown" contains a sample of "Solid As A Rock" performed by <a href="/wiki/Sizzla" title="Sizzla">Sizzla</a>.</li>
<li>"Heaven" contains a sample of "Reverie" by <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Younge" title="Adrian Younge">Adrian Younge</a>, and lyrically samples "<a href="/wiki/Losing_My_Religion" title="Losing My Religion">Losing My Religion</a>" by <a href="/wiki/R.E.M." title="R.E.M.">R.E.M.</a><sup id="cite_ref-complex1_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex1-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"Versus" embodies portions of <a href="/wiki/A_Tribe_Called_Quest" title="A Tribe Called Quest">A Tribe Called Quest</a>'s "Sucka Nigga".<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"Part II (On the Run)" contains a sample of "Believe in Me" by <a href="/wiki/One_Way_(American_band)" title="One Way (American band)">One Way</a>.</li>
<li>"BBC" lyrically samples "<a href="/wiki/Feel_So_Good_(song)" title="Feel So Good (song)">Feel So Good</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Mase" title="Mase">Mase</a>.</li>
<li>"Jay Z Blue" contains samples from "My Downfall" by <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a> and a monologue by <a href="/wiki/Faye_Dunaway" title="Faye Dunaway">Faye Dunaway</a> in the 1981 film <i><a href="/wiki/Mommie_Dearest_(film)" title="Mommie Dearest (film)">Mommie Dearest</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>"Nickels and Dimes" contains a sample of "Nikels and Dimes" performed by <a href="/wiki/Gonjasufi" title="Gonjasufi">Gonjasufi</a>.</li>
</ul>
